State Locking\\n33: \\n34: The S3 backend now supports S3 native state locking as an opt-in, experimental feature.\\n35: An S3 lock can be used alongside a DynamoDB lock, or independently.\\n36: When both locking mechanisms are configured, a lock must be successfully acquired from both locations before subsequent operations will proceed.\\n37: \\n38: To opt-in to S3 native state locking, set `use_lockfile` to `true`.\\n39: \\n40: ```terraform\\n41: terraform {\\n42:   backend \\\"s3\\\" {\\n43:     # additional configuration omitted for brevity\\n44:     use_lockfile = true\\n45:   }\\n46: }\\n47: ```\\n48: \\n49: With S3 locking enabled, a lock file will be placed in the same location as the state file.\\n50: The lock file will be named identically to the state file, but with a `.tflock` extension.\\n51: **S3 bucket policies and IAM policies attached to the calling principal may need to be adjusted to include permissions for the new lock file.**\\n52: \\n53: In a future minor version of Terraform the experimental label will be removed from the `use_lockfile` attribute and attributes related to DynamoDB based locking will be deprecated.\\n54: \\n55: ### Root Assume Role Attribute Removal\\n56: \\n57: Several root level attributes related to IAM role assumption which were previously deprecated have been removed.\\n58: Each removed field has an analogous field \\n30: ## S3 Backend \\n31: \\n32: ### S3 Native State Locking\\n33: \\n34: The S3 backend now supports S3 native state locking as an opt-in, experimental feature.\\n35: An S3 lock can be used omitted for brevity\\n44:     use_lockfile = true\\n45:   }\\n46: }\\n47: ```\\n48: \\n49: With S3 locking enabled, a lock file will be placed in the same location as the state file.\\n50: The lock file will be named identically to the state file, but with a `.tflock` extension.\\n51: **S3 bucket policies and IAM policies attached to the calling principal may need to be adjusted to include permissions for the new lock file.**\\n52: \\n53: In a future minor version of Terraform the experimental label will be removed from the `use_lockfile` attribute and attributes related to DynamoDB based locking will be deprecated.\\n54: \\n55: ### Root Assume Role Attribute Removal\\n56: \\n57: Several root level attributes related to IAM role assumption which were previously deprecated have been removed.\\n58: Each removed field has an analogous field inside the [`assume_role` block](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/backend/s3#assume-role-configuration) which should be \n30: ## S3 Backend \n31: \n32: ### S3 Native State Locking\n33: \n34: The S3 backend now supports S3 native state locking as an opt-in, experimental feature.\n35: An S3 lock can be used alongside a DynamoDB lock, or independently.\n36: When both locking mechanisms are configured, a lock must be successfully acquired from both locations before subsequent operations will proceed.\n37: \n38: To opt-in to S3 native state locking, set `use_lockfile` to `true`.\n39: \n40: ```terraform\n41: terraform {\n42:   backend \"s3\" {\n43:     # additional configuration omitted for brevity\n44:     use_lockfile = true\n45:   }\n46: }\n47: ```\n48: \n49: With S3 locking enabled, a lock file will be placed in the same location as the state file.\n50: The lock file will be named identically to the state file, but with a `.tflock` extension.\n51: **S3 bucket policies and IAM policies attached to the calling principal may need to be adjusted to include permissions for the new lock file.**\n52: \n53: In a future minor version of Terraform the experimental label will be removed from the `use_lockfile` attribute and attributes related to DynamoDB based locking will be deprecated.\n54: \n55: ### Root Assume Role Attribute Removal\n56: \n57: Several root level attributes related to IAM role assumption which were previously deprecated have been removed.\n58: Each removed field has an analogous field inside the [`assume_role` block](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/backend/s3#assume-role-configuration) which should be used instead.\n59: \n60: | Removed | Ephemeral resources always produce ephemeral values.\\n5:  - **Ephemeral values**: Input variables and outputs can now be defined as ephemeral. Ephemeral values may only be used in certain contexts in Terraform configuration, and are not persisted to the plan or state files.\\n6:     - **`ephemeralasnull` function**: a function takes a value of any type and returns a similar value of the same type with any ephemeral values replaced with non-ephemeral null values and all non-ephemeral values preserved.\\n7: \\n8: BUG FIXES:\\n9: \\n10: - The `secret_suffix` in the `kubernetes` backend now includes validation to prevent errors when the `secret_suffix` ends with a number ([#35666](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35666)).\\n11: - The error message for an invalid default value for an input variable now indicates when the problem is with a nested value in a complex data type. ([#35465](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35465))\\n12: - Sensitive marks could be incorrectly transferred to nested resource values, causing erroneous changes during a plan ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n13: - Allow unknown `error_message` values to pass the core validate step, so variable validation can be completed later during plan\\n14:   ([#35537](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35537))\\n15: - Unencoded slashes within GitHub module source refs were being truncated and incorrectly used as subdirectories in the request path ([#35552](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35552))\\n16: - Terraform refresh-only plans with output only changes are now applyable. ([#35812](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35812))\\n17: - Postconditions referencing `self` with many instances could encounter an error during evaluation ([#35895](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35895))\\n18: - The `plantimestamp()` function would return an invalid date during validation ([#35902](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35902))\\n19: - Updates to resources which were forced to use create_before_destroy could lose that flag in the state temporarily and cause cycles if immediately removed from the configuration ([#35966](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35966))\\n20: - backend/cloud: Prefer KV tags, even when tags are defined as set ([#35937](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35937))\\n21: - Simplify config generation (`plan -generate-config-out`) for string attributes that contain primitive types (e.g. numbers or booleans) ([#35984](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35984))\\n22: - config: `issensitive` could incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later became sensitive during apply, causing failures where changes did not match the planned result ([#36012](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36012))\\n23: - config: The evaluation of conditional expressions and for expression in HCL could lose marks with certain combinations of unknown values ([#36017](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36017))\\n24: \\n25: ENHANCEMENTS:\\n26: \\n27: - The `element` function now accepts negative indices ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n28: - Import block validation has been improved to provide more useful errors and catch more invalid cases during `terraform validate` ([#35543](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35543))\\n29: - Performance enhancements for resource evaluation, especially when large numbers of resource instances are involved ([#35558](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35558))\\n30: - The `plan`, `apply`, and `refresh` commands now produce a deprecated warning when using the `-state` flag. Instead use the `path` attribute within the `local` backend to modify the state file. ([#35660](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35660))\\n31: - backend/cos: Add new auth for Tencent Cloud backend ([#35888](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35888))\\n32: \\n33: UPGRADE NOTES:\\n34: \\n35: - backend/s3: Removes deprecated attributes for assuming IAM role. Must use the `assume_role` block ([#35721](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35721))\\n36: - backend/s3: The s3 backend now supports S3 native state locking. When used with DynamoDB-based locking, locks will be acquired from both sources. In a future minor release of Terraform the DynamoDB locking mechanism and associated arguments will be deprecated. ([#35661](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35661))\\n37: - `moved`: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and keywords from `moved` blocks will need to prepend the `resource.` identifier to these references. ([#35850](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35850))\\n38: - config: In order to ensure consistency in results from HCL conditional expressions, marks must be combined from all values within the expression to avoid losing mark information. This typically improves accuracy when validating configuration, but users may see sensitive results where they were lost previously.\\n39: \\n40: ## Previous Releases\\n41: \\n42: For information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\\n43: \\n44: - Ephemeral values may only be used in certain contexts in Terraform configuration, and are not persisted to the plan or state files.\n6:     - **`ephemeralasnull` function**: a function takes a value of any type and returns a similar value of the same type with any ephemeral values replaced with non-ephemeral null values and all non-ephemeral values preserved.\n7: \n8: BUG FIXES:\n9: \n10: - The `secret_suffix` in the `kubernetes` backend now includes validation to prevent errors when the `secret_suffix` ends with a number ([#35666](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35666)).\n11: - The error message for an invalid default value for an input variable now indicates when the problem is with a nested value in a complex data type. ([#35812](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35812))\n17: - Postconditions referencing `self` with many instances could encounter an error during evaluation ([#35895](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35895))\n18: - The `plantimestamp()` function would return an invalid date during validation ([#35902](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35902))\n19: - Updates to resources which were forced to use create_before_destroy could lose that flag in the state temporarily and cause cycles if immediately removed from the configuration ([#35966](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35966))\n20: - backend/cloud: Prefer KV tags, even when tags are defined as set ([#35937](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35937))\n21: - Simplify config generation (`plan -generate-config-out`) for string attributes that contain primitive types (e.g. numbers or booleans) ([#35984](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35984))\n22: - config: `issensitive` could incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later became sensitive during apply, causing failures where changes did not match the planned result ([#36012](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36012))\n23: - config: The evaluation of conditional expressions and for expression in HCL could lose marks with certain combinations of unknown values ([#36017](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36017))\n24: \n25: ENHANCEMENTS:\n26: \n27: - The `element` function now accepts negative indices ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\n28: - Import block validation has been improved to provide more useful errors and catch more invalid cases during `terraform validate` ([#35543](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35543))\n29: - Performance enhancements for resource evaluation, especially when large numbers of resource instances are involved ([#35558](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35558))\n30: - The `plan`, `apply`, and `refresh` commands now produce a deprecated warning when using the `-state` flag. Instead use the `path` attribute within the `local` backend to modify the state file. ([#35660](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35660))\n31: - backend/cos: Add new auth for Tencent Cloud backend ([#35888](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35888))\n32: \n33: UPGRADE NOTES:\n34: \n35: - backend/s3: Removes deprecated attributes for assuming IAM role. Must use the `assume_role` block ([#35721](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35721))\n36: - backend/s3: The s3 backend now supports S3 native state locking. When used with DynamoDB-based locking, locks will be acquired from both sources. In a future minor release of Terraform the DynamoDB locking mechanism and associated arguments will be deprecated. ([#35661](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35661))\n37: - `moved`: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and keywords from `moved` blocks will need to prepend the `resource.` identifier to these references. ([#35850](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35850))\n38: - config: In order to ensure consistency in results from HCL conditional expressions, marks must be combined from all values within the expression to avoid losing mark information. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_017ztHDWwpSZitGQ8ymmVc34","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: ---\\n2: page_title: 'Backend Type: s3'\\n3: description: Terraform can store state remotely in S3 and lock that state with DynamoDB.\\n4: ---\\n5: \\n6: # S3\\n7: \\n8: Stores the state as a given key in a given bucket on [Amazon S3](https://aws.amazon.com/s3/).\\n9: This backend also supports state locking and consistency checking via [Dynamo DB](https://aws.amazon.com/dynamodb/), which can be enabled by setting the `dynamodb_table` field to an existing DynamoDB table name.\\n10: A single DynamoDB table can be used to lock multiple remote state files.\\n11: Terraform generates key names that include the values of the `bucket` and `key` variables.\\n12: \\n13: ~> **Warning!** It is highly recommended that you enable\\n14: [Bucket Versioning](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/manage-versioning-examples.html)\\n15: on the S3 bucket to allow for state recovery in the case of accidental deletions and human error.\\n16: \\n17: ## Example Configuration\\n18: \\n19: ```hcl\\n20: terraform {\\n21:   backend \\\"s3\\\" {\\n22:     bucket = \\\"example-bucket\\\"\\n23:     key    = \\\"path/to/state\\\"\\n24:     region = \\\"us-east-1\\\"\\n25:   }\\n26: }\\n27: ```\\n28: \\n29: This assumes we have a bucket created called `mybucket`. The Terraform state is written to the key `path/to/my/key`.\\n30: \\n31: Note that for the access credentials we recommend using a [partial configuration](/terraform/language/backend#partial-configuration).\\n32: \\n33: ## State Storage\\n34: \\n35: The S3 backend stores state data in an S3 object at the path set by the `key` parameter in the S3 bucket indicated by the `bucket` parameter.\\n36: Using the example shown above, the state would be stored at the path `path/to/my/key` in the bucket `mybucket`.\\n37: \\n38: When using [workspaces](/terraform/language/state/workspaces), the state for the `default` workspace is stored at the location described above.\\n39: Other workspaces are stored using the path `<workspace_key_prefix>/<workspace_name>/<key>`.\\n40: The default workspace key prefix is `env:` and it can be configured using the parameter `workspace_key_prefix`.\\n41: Using the example above, the state for the workspace `development` would be stored at the path `env:/development/path/to/my/key`.\\n42: \\n43: ## Permissions Required\\n44: \\n45: ### S3 Bucket Permissions\\n46: \\n47: When not using [workspaces](/terraform/language/state/workspaces)(or when only using the `default` workspace), Terraform will need the following AWS IAM permissions on the target backend bucket:\\n48: \\n49: * `s3:ListBucket` on `arn:aws:s3:::mybucket`. At a minimum, this must be able to list the path where the state is stored.\\n50: * `s3:GetObject` on `arn:aws:s3:::mybucket/path/to/my/key`\\n51: * `s3:PutObject` on `arn:aws:s3:::mybucket/path/to/my/key`\\n52: \\n53: Note: `s3:DeleteObject` is not needed, as Terraform will not delete the state storage.\\n54: \\n55: This is seen in the following AWS IAM Statement:\\n56: \\n57: ```json\\n58: {\\n59:   \\\"Version\\\": \\\"2012-10-17\\\",\\n60:   \\\"Statement\\\": [\\n61:     {\\n62:       \\\"Effect\\\": \\\"Allow\\\",\\n63:       \\\"Action\\\": \\\"s3:ListBucket\\\",\\n64:       \\\"Resource\\\": \\\"arn:aws:s3:::mybucket\\\"\\n65:     },\\n66:     {\\n67:       \\\"Effect\\\": \\\"Allow\\\",\\n68:       \\\"Action\\\": [\\\"s3:GetObject\\\", \\\"s3:PutObject\\\"],\\n69:       \\\"Resource\\\": \\\"arn:aws:s3:::mybucket/path/to/my/key\\\"\\n70:     }\\n71:   ]\\n72: }\\n73: ```\\n74: \\n75: When using [workspaces](/terraform/language/state/workspaces), Terraform will also need permissions to create, list, read, update, and delete the workspace state storage:\\n76: \\n77: * `s3:ListBucket` on `arn:aws:s3:::mybucket`. At a minumum, this must be able to list the path where the `default` workspace is stored as well as the other workspaces.\\n78: * `s3:GetObject` on `arn:aws:s3:::mybucket/path/to/my/key` and `arn:aws:s3:::mybucket/<workspace_key_prefix>/*/path/to/my/key`\\n79: * `s3:PutObject` on `arn:aws:s3:::mybucket/path/to/my/key` and `arn:aws:s3:::mybucket/<workspace_key_prefix>/*/path/to/my/key`\\n80: * `s3:DeleteObject` on `arn:aws:s3:::mybucket/<workspace_key_prefix>/*/path/to/my/key`\\n81: \\n82: -> **Note:** AWS can control access to S3 buckets with either IAM policies\\n83: attached to users/groups/roles (like the example above) or resource policies\\n84: attached to bucket objects (which look similar but also require a `Principal` to\\n85: indicate which entity has those permissions). (Optional) Custom endpoint URL for the AWS STS API.\\n229:   This can also be sourced from the environment variable `AWS_ENDPOINT_URL_STS` or the deprecated environment variable `AWS_STS_ENDPOINT`.\\n230: \\n231: The environment variable `AWS_ENDPOINT_URL` can be used to set a base endpoint URL for all services.\\n232: \\n233: Endpoints can also be overridden using the [AWS shared configuration file](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/sdkref/latest/guide/feature-ss-endpoints.html#ss-endpoints-config).\\n234: Setting the parameter `endpoint_url` on a profile will set that endpoint for all services.\\n235: To set endpoints for specific services, create a `services` section and set the `endpoint_url` parameters for each desired service.\\n236: Endpoints set for specific services will override the base endpoint configured in the profile.\\n237: \\n238: #### Assume Role Configuration\\n239: \\n240: The argument `assume_role` contains the following arguments:\\n241: \\n242: * `role_arn` - (Required) Amazon Resource Name (ARN) of the IAM Role to assume.\\n243: * `duration` - (Optional) The duration individual credentials will be valid.\\n244:   Credentials are automatically renewed up to the maximum defined by the AWS account.\\n245:   Specified using the format `<hours>h<minutes>m<seconds>s` with any unit being optional.\\n246:   For example, an hour and a half can be specified as `1h30m` or `90m`. \\n247:   Must be between 15 minutes (15m) and 12 hours (12h).\\n248: * `external_id` - (Optional) External identifier to use when assuming the role.\\n249: * `policy` - (Optional) IAM Policy JSON describing further restricting permissions for the IAM Role being assumed.\\n250: * `policy_arns` - (Optional) Set of Amazon Resource Names (ARNs) of IAM Policies describing further restricting permissions for the IAM Role being assumed.\\n251: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/terraform--24236f4f@e1a7505de5f9af1ffec8078d6baa58426aa7c353/-/blob/website/docs/language/backend/s3.mdx%3FL100-250\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"100: \n101: ```json\n102: {\n103:   \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n104:   \"Statement\": [\n105:     {\n106:       \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n107:       \"Action\": [\n108:         \"dynamodb:DescribeTable\",\n109:         \"dynamodb:GetItem\",\n110:         \"dynamodb:PutItem\",\n111:         \"dynamodb:DeleteItem\"\n112:       ],\n113:       \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:dynamodb:*:*:table/mytable\"\n114:     }\n115:   ]\n116: }\n117: ```\n118: \n119: ## Data Source Configuration\n120: \n121: To make use of the S3 remote state in another configuration,\n122: use the [`terraform_remote_state` data source](/terraform/language/state/remote-state-data).\n123: \n124: ```hcl\n125: data \"terraform_remote_state\" \"network\" {\n126:   backend = \"s3\"\n127:   config = {\n128:     bucket = \"terraform-state-prod\"\n129:     key    = \"network/terraform.tfstate\"\n130:     region = \"us-east-1\"\n131:   }\n132: }\n133: ```\n134: \n135: The `terraform_remote_state` data source will return all of the root module\n136: outputs defined in the referenced remote state (but not any outputs from\n137: nested modules unless they are explicitly output again in the root). An\n138: example output might look like:\n139: \n140: ```\n141: data.terraform_remote_state.network:\n142:   id = 2016-10-29 01:57:59.780010914 +0000 UTC\n143:   addresses.# = 2\n144:   addresses.0 = 52.207.220.222\n145:   addresses.1 = 54.196.78.166\n146:   backend = s3\n147:   config.% = 3\n148:   config.bucket = terraform-state-prod\n149:   config.key = network/terraform.tfstate\n150:   config.region = us-east-1\n151:   elb_address = web-elb-790251200.us-east-1.elb.amazonaws.com\n152:   public_subnet_id = subnet-1e05dd33\n153: ```\n154: \n155: ## Configuration\n156: \n157: This backend requires the configuration of the AWS Region and S3 state storage. Other configuration, such as enabling DynamoDB state locking, is optional.\n158: \n159: ### Credentials and Shared Configuration\n160: \n161: !> **Warning:**  We recommend using environment variables to supply credentials and other sensitive data. If you use `-backend-config` or hardcode these values directly in your configuration, Terraform will include these values in both the `.terraform` subdirectory and in plan files. Refer to [Credentials and Sensitive Data](/terraform/language/backend#credentials-and-sensitive-data) for details.\n162: \n163: The following configuration is required:\n164: \n165: * `region` - (Required) AWS Region of the S3 Bucket and DynamoDB Table (if used). This can also be sourced from the `AWS_DEFAULT_REGION` and `AWS_REGION` environment variables.\n166: \n167: The following configuration is optional:\n168: \n169: * `use_lockfile` - (Experimental, Optional) Whether to use a lockfile for locking the state file. Defaults to `false`.\n170: * `access_key` - (Optional) AWS access key. If configured, must also configure `secret_key`. This can also be sourced from the `AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID` environment variable, AWS shared credentials file (e.g. `~/.aws/credentials`), or AWS shared configuration file (e.g. `~/.aws/config`).\n171: * `allowed_account_ids` - (Optional) List of allowed AWS account IDs to prevent potential destruction of a live environment. Conflicts with `forbidden_account_ids`.\n172: * `custom_ca_bundle` - (Optional) File containing custom root and intermediate certificates. Can also be set using the `AWS_CA_BUNDLE` environment variable. Setting ca_bundle in the shared config file is not supported.\n173: * `ec2_metadata_service_endpoint` - (Optional) Custom endpoint URL for the EC2 Instance Metadata Service (IMDS) API.\n174:   Can also be set with the `AWS_EC2_METADATA_SERVICE_ENDPOINT` environment variable.\n175: * `ec2_metadata_service_endpoint_mode` - (Optional) Mode to use in communicating with the metadata service.\n176:   Valid values are `IPv4` and `IPv6`.\n177:   Can also be set with the `AWS_EC2_METADATA_SERVICE_ENDPOINT_MODE` environment variable.\n178: * `forbidden_account_ids` - (Optional) List of forbidden AWS account IDs to prevent potential destruction of a live environment. Conflicts with `allowed_account_ids`.\n179: * `http_proxy` - (Optional) URL of a proxy to use for HTTP requests when accessing the AWS API.\n180:   Can also be set using the `HTTP_PROXY` or `http_proxy` environment variables.\n181: * `https_proxy` - (Optional) URL of a proxy to use for HTTPS requests when accessing the AWS API.\n182:   Can also be set using the `HTTPS_PROXY` or `https_proxy` environment variables.\n183: * `iam_endpoint` - (Optional, **Deprecated**) Custom endpoint URL for the AWS Identity and Access Management (IAM) API.\n184:   Use `endpoints.iam` instead.\n185: * `insecure` - (Optional) Whether to explicitly allow the backend to perform \"insecure\" SSL requests. If omitted, the default value is `false`.\n186: * `no_proxy` - (Optional) Comma-separated list of hosts that should not use HTTP or HTTPS proxies.\n187:   Each value can be one of:\n188:     * A domain name\n189:     * An IP address\n190:     * A CIDR address\n191:     * An asterisk (`*`), to indicate that no proxying should be performed\n192:   Domain name and IP address values can also include a port number.\n193:   Can also be set using the `NO_PROXY` or `no_proxy` environment variables.\n194: * `max_retries` - (Optional) The maximum number of times an AWS API request is retried on retryable failure. Defaults to 5.\n195: * `profile` - (Optional) Name of AWS profile in AWS shared credentials file (e.g. `~/.aws/credentials`) or AWS shared configuration file (e.g. `~/.aws/config`) to use for credentials and/or configuration. This can also be sourced from the `AWS_PROFILE` environment variable.\n196: * `retry_mode` - (Optional) Specifies how retries are attempted. Valid values are `standard` and `adaptive`. Can also be configured using the `AWS_RETRY_MODE` environment variable or the shared config file parameter `retry_mode`.\n197: * `secret_key` - (Optional) AWS access key. If configured, must also configure `access_key`. This can also be sourced from the `AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY` environment variable, AWS shared credentials file (e.g. `~/.aws/credentials`), or AWS shared configuration file (e.g. `~/.aws/config`).\n198: * `shared_config_files`  - (Optional) List of paths to AWS shared configuration files. Defaults to `~/.aws/config`.\n199: * `shared_credentials_file`  - (Optional, **Deprecated**, use `shared_credentials_files` instead) Path to the AWS shared credentials file. Defaults to `~/.aws/credentials`.\n200: * `shared_credentials_files`  - (Optional) List of paths to AWS shared credentials files. Defaults to `~/.aws/credentials`.\n201: * `skip_credentials_validation` - (Optional) Skip credentials validation via the STS API.\n202:   Useful for testing and for AWS API implementations that do not have STS available.\n203: * `skip_region_validation` - (Optional) Skip validation of provided region name.\n204: * `skip_requesting_account_id` - (Optional) Whether to skip requesting the account ID.\n205:   Useful for AWS API implementations that do not have the IAM, STS API, or metadata API.\n206: * `skip_metadata_api_check` - (Optional) Skip usage of EC2 Metadata API.\n207: * `skip_s3_checksum` - (Optional) Do not include checksum when uploading S3 Objects.\n208:   Useful for some S3-Compatible APIs.\n209: * `sts_endpoint` - (Optional, **Deprecated**) Custom endpoint URL for the AWS Security Token Service (STS) API.\n210:   Use `endpoints.sts` instead.\n211: * `sts_region` - (Optional) AWS region for STS. If unset, AWS will use the same region for STS as other non-STS operations.\n212: * `token` - (Optional) Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) token. This can also be sourced from the `AWS_SESSION_TOKEN` environment variable.\n213: * `use_dualstack_endpoint` - (Optional) Force the backend to resolve endpoints with DualStack capability. Can also be set with the `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variable or in a shared config file (`use_dualstack_endpoint`).\n214: * `use_fips_endpoint` - (Optional) Force the backend to resolve endpoints with FIPS capability. Can also be set with the `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` environment variable or in a shared config file (`use_fips_endpoint`).\n215: \n216: #### Overriding AWS API endpoints\n217: \n218: The optional argument `endpoints` contains the following arguments:\n219: \n220: * `dynamodb` - {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01CiwbsnY6JxajS1QKfL8hov","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: ---\\n2: page_title: Upgrading to Terraform v1.10\\n3: description: Upgrading to Terraform v1.10\\n4: ---\\n5: \\n6: # Upgrading to Terraform v1.10\\n7: \\n8: -> **Tip:** Use the version selector to view the upgrade guides for older Terraform versions.\\n9: \\n10: Terraform v1.10 is a minor release in the stable Terraform v1.0 series.\\n11: \\n12: Terraform v1.10 honors the\\n13: [Terraform v1.0 Compatibility Promises](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1-compatibility-promises).\\n14: There are minor changes that may require additional upgrade steps:\\n15: \\n16: - `moved` blocks will now report an error if `from` or `to` points to a resource type conflicting with reserved keywords\\n17: \\n18: See [the full changelog](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\\n19: for more details. If you encounter any problems during upgrading which are not\\n20: covered this guide, please start a new topic in\\n21: [the Terraform community forum](https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core)\\n22: to discuss it.\\n23: \\n24: ## Conflicting `moved` block references\\n25: \\n26: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords such as `local`, `each`, `self` etc. when parsing resource addresses.\\n27: Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and\\n28: keywords from moved blocks will need to prepend the reference identifier with `resource.`.\\n29: \\n30: ## S3 Backend \\n31: \\n32: ### S3 Native State Locking\\n33: \\n34: The S3 backend now supports S3 native state locking as an opt-in, experimental feature.\\n35: An S3 lock can be used alongside a DynamoDB lock, or independently.\\n36: When both locking mechanisms are configured, a lock must be successfully acquired from both locations before subsequent operations will proceed.\\n37: \\n38: To opt-in to S3 native state locking, set `use_lockfile` to `true`.\\n39: \\n40: ```terraform\\n41: terraform {\\n42:   backend \\\"s3\\\" {\\n43:     # additional configuration omitted for brevity\\n44:     use_lockfile = true\\n45:   }\\n46: }\\n47: ```\\n48: \\n49: With S3 locking enabled, a lock file will be placed in the same location as the state file.\\n50: The lock file will be named identically to the state file, but with a `.tflock` extension.\\n51: **S3 bucket policies and IAM policies attached to the calling principal may need to be adjusted to include permissions for the new lock file.**\\n52: \\n53: In a future minor version of Terraform the experimental label will be removed from the `use_lockfile` attribute and attributes related to DynamoDB based locking will be deprecated.\\n54: \\n55: ### Root Assume Role Attribute Removal\\n56: \\n57: Several root level attributes related to IAM role {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01SX7WR4hu5mn48LefvVSdt9","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01HP2pL2rzVPoKHdJB2hc1R1","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide\n\n**Release Date:** November 27, 2024\n\nThis guide provides step-by-step instructions for upgrading from Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0. While v1.10.0 honors the [Terraform v1.0 Compatibility Promises](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1-compatibility-promises), there are several breaking changes and behavioral modifications that require migration steps.\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces two major new features with migration implications:\n- **Ephemeral Resources and Values**: A new mechanism for handling secrets and temporary data that isn't persisted to state files\n- **Enhanced Sensitive Value Handling**: Improvements to how sensitive marks propagate through conditional and for expressions\n\nIt also includes breaking changes to the S3 backend and moved block syntax that require configuration updates.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Assumption Attributes\n\n#### What Changed and Why\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 **removes** the root-level IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend that were previously marked as deprecated. These attributes have been entirely removed in favor of the `assume_role` block syntax, which provides a cleaner, more organized way to configure role assumption.\n\n**Removed attributes:**\n- `role_arn`\n- `session_name`\n- `external_id`\n- `assume_role_duration_seconds`\n- `assume_role_policy`\n- `assume_role_policy_arns`\n- `assume_role_tags`\n- `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys`\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket                        = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key                           = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region                        = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table                = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    # DEPRECATED - These attributes must be migrated\n    role_arn                       = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n    session_name                   = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id                    = \"unique-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds   = 3600\n    assume_role_policy            = jsonencode({\n      Version = \"2012-10-17\"\n      Statement = [...]\n    })\n    assume_role_tags              = {\n      Environment = \"production\"\n    }\n    assume_role_transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    # Use the assume_role block instead\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn           = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n      session_name       = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id        = \"unique-external-id\"\n      duration           = \"1h\"  # Note: format changed from seconds to duration string\n      policy            = jsonencode({\n        Version = \"2012-10-17\"\n        Statement = [...]\n      })\n      policy_arn = [\n        \"arn:aws:iam::aws:policy/ReadOnlyAccess\"\n      ]\n      tags = {\n        Environment = \"production\"\n      }\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Back up your state file** before proceeding:\n   ```bash\n   terraform state pull > terraform.tfstate.backup\n   ```\n\n2. **Update your S3 backend configuration**:\n   - Remove all root-level `role_arn`, `session_name`, `external_id`, `assume_role_*` attributes\n   - Create an `assume_role` block containing the equivalent settings\n   - Convert `assume_role_duration_seconds` to duration format:\n     - `3600` (seconds) → `1h` (1 hour)\n     - Use format: `<hours>h<minutes>m<seconds>s`\n\n3. **Replace array attributes correctly**:\n   - `assume_role_policy_arns` (set) → `policy_arn` (list)\n   - `assume_role_tags` → `tags`\n\n4. **Validate your configuration**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform init\n   terraform validate\n   ```\n\n5. **Run a plan to ensure nothing changes unexpectedly**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Duration format**: Don't use raw seconds in the `duration` field - use the `1h` format instead\n- **Forgetting `assume_role` block**: If you remove the old attributes but don't add the `assume_role` block, Terraform will fail to initialize\n- **IAM permissions**: Ensure your IAM policies are updated to include `sts:AssumeRole` permissions for the role specified in `assume_role.role_arn`\n\n---\n\n### 2. S3 Backend: New S3 Native State Locking Support\n\n#### What Changed\n\nThe S3 backend now supports S3 native state locking as an **opt-in, experimental feature**. This allows locking state directly in S3 without requiring a separate DynamoDB table.\n\n#### Key Points\n\n- **Opt-in via `use_lockfile` parameter**: Set to `true` to enable S3 native locking\n- **Works alongside DynamoDB**: When both are configured, locks are acquired from both sources\n- **Lock file naming**: Lock files are stored with `.tflock` extension (e.g., `prod/terraform.tfstate.tflock`)\n- **IAM policy updates needed**: S3 bucket and IAM policies must be updated to include permissions for the lock files\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"  # Only option\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n**Option A: Use S3 native locking only (experimental)**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket       = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key          = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region       = \"us-east-1\"\n    use_lockfile = true  # New experimental feature\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Option B: Use both S3 and DynamoDB locking**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n    use_lockfile   = true  # Locks acquired from both sources\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps (Optional)\n\nTo adopt S3 native locking:\n\n1. **Update your S3 bucket policy** to include lock file permissions:\n   ```json\n   {\n     \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n     \"Statement\": [\n       {\n         \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n         \"Action\": [\n           \"s3:GetObject\",\n           \"s3:PutObject\",\n           \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n         ],\n         \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state/path/to/*.tflock\"\n       }\n     ]\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Update IAM policy** for your Terraform user/role:\n   ```json\n   {\n     \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n     \"Statement\": [\n       {\n         \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n         \"Action\": [\n           \"s3:GetObject\",\n           \"s3:PutObject\",\n           \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n         ],\n         \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state/path/to/*.tflock\"\n       }\n     ]\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Enable in your backend configuration**:\n   ```hcl\n   terraform {\n     backend \"s3\" {\n       # ... existing config ...\n       use_lockfile = true\n     }\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Run init and plan**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform init\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n#### Important Notes\n\n- This feature is **experimental** - behavior may change in future minor releases\n- DynamoDB-based locking will be deprecated in a future minor release\n- Both locking mechanisms can be used together for gradual migration\n\n---\n\n### 3. Moved Blocks: Syntax Changes for Reserved Keywords\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 enforces stricter parsing of resource addresses in `moved` blocks. Resources with type names that match reserved keywords (like `local`, `each`, `self`, `data`, `resource`, `module`, `variable`, `output`, `terraform`, `provider`) must now be prefixed with `resource.` to disambiguate them from the reserved keywords.\n\n#### Why This Matters\n\nPreviously, you could write:\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = local.my_resource\n  to   = aws_instance.web\n}\n```\n\nHowever, this creates ambiguity: Is `local` referring to a local value or a resource type named `local`? Terraform v1.10.0 requires explicit disambiguation.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\n# If you had a resource with type name matching a keyword\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  # ...\n}\n\n# This was ambiguous - did you mean the resource or the keyword?\nmoved {\n  from = local.config  # Ambiguous!\n  to   = aws_instance.web\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\n# Same resource\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  # ...\n}\n\n# Now you must be explicit\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.config  # Clear that this is a resource\n  to   = aws_instance.web\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Identify problematic `moved` blocks**: Check your configuration for `moved` blocks where the resource type matches a reserved keyword:\n   - `local`, `each`, `self`, `data`, `resource`, `module`, `variable`, `output`, `terraform`, `provider`\n\n2. **Add `resource.` prefix**: For any `from` or `to` addresses using reserved keyword resource types, prepend `resource.`:\n   ```hcl\n   # BEFORE\n   moved {\n     from = local.example\n     to   = aws_instance.web\n   }\n\n   # AFTER\n   moved {\n     from = resource.local.example\n     to   = aws_instance.web\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Validate your configuration**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   ```\n\n4. **Common reserved keywords to watch for**:\n   - `local` - Most common\n   - `data` - Data source type\n   - `resource` - Resource keyword\n   - `module` - Module keyword\n   - `variable`, `output` - Variable and output keywords\n   - `terraform`, `provider` - Meta-block keywords\n   - `each`, `self` - Built-in variables\n\n#### Example Scenario\n\nIf your codebase had custom providers with these type names:\n\n```hcl\n# Before migration - breaks in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = local.my_resource\n  to   = aws_instance.new_resource\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = data.old_config\n  to   = local_file.new_config\n}\n\n# After migration - works in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.my_resource\n  to   = aws_instance.new_resource\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = resource.data.old_config\n  to   = local_file.new_config\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### 4. Ephemeral Resources and Values\n\n#### What Are Ephemeral Values?\n\nEphemeral values are data that exists during Terraform operations but is **never stored** in plan files or state files. This is ideal for secrets, API tokens, and temporary credentials that should not persist beyond the current operation.\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n- **Not persisted**: Never written to `.tfstate` or plan files\n- **Temporary**: Available only during the current operation\n- **Contextual**: Can only be referenced in specific \"ephemeral contexts\"\n- **Secure by design**: Secrets are never at rest\n\n#### New Features in v1.10.0\n\n**1. Ephemeral Input Variables**\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_token\" {\n  type        = string\n  ephemeral   = true\n  description = \"Temporary API token that won't be stored in state\"\n}\n```\n\n**2. Ephemeral Outputs (in child modules)**\n```hcl\noutput \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  value       = aws_iam_access_key.temp.secret_access_key\n  ephemeral   = true\n  description = \"Temporary AWS secret key not stored in state\"\n}\n```\n\n**3. Ephemeral Resources**\n```hcl\nephemeral \"random_password\" \"temp\" {\n  length  = 32\n  special = true\n}\n```\n\n**4. `ephemeralasnull()` Function**\n```hcl\n# Convert ephemeral values to null for contexts where ephemeral isn't allowed\nlocal_file.config = {\n  content = ephemeralasnull(var.sensitive_config)\n}\n```\n\n#### Valid Contexts for Ephemeral Values\n\nEphemeral variables can only be referenced in:\n- Other ephemeral variables\n- Ephemeral local values\n- Ephemeral resources\n- Ephemeral outputs\n- `provider` blocks (for configuring providers)\n- `provisioner` and `connection` blocks\n\n#### Migration Considerations\n\n**If you currently use `sensitive` for secrets:**\n```hcl\n# v1.9.0 approach - secrets stored in state (marked as sensitive in output)\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true  # Hidden in output, but still in state\n}\n```\n\n**Consider migrating to ephemeral if the secret never needs to be stored:**\n```hcl\n# v1.10.0 approach - secrets never stored at all\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type        = string\n  ephemeral   = true  # Not stored in state or plan\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps for Ephemeral Values\n\n1. **Identify secrets that don't need persistence**: Look for resources/variables that only need to exist during execution\n2. **Mark them as ephemeral** where appropriate:\n   ```hcl\n   # Before\n   variable \"temporary_token\" {\n     type      = string\n     sensitive = true\n   }\n\n   # After\n   variable \"temporary_token\" {\n     type      = string\n     ephemeral = true\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Update references to respect ephemeral contexts**: If you reference ephemeral values outside of valid contexts, use `ephemeralasnull()`:\n   ```hcl\n   resource \"aws_instance\" \"web\" {\n     # This would fail - can't use ephemeral variable directly here\n     # user_data = var.temp_token\n\n     # Instead, handle gracefully\n     user_data = base64encode(ephemeralasnull(var.temp_token) ?? \"\")\n   }\n   ```\n\n#### Important Notes\n\n- **Ephemeral is in public beta**: Workflows are subject to change\n- **Root module limitation**: You cannot mark outputs as ephemeral in the root module\n- **Ephemeral outputs are child-module only**: Can only be used to pass values between modules, not persisted to root module state\n\n---\n\n### 5. Sensitive Value Handling in Conditional Expressions\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 **improves the consistency** of how sensitive marks propagate through conditional expressions. Previously, sensitive marks could be lost in certain combinations of conditional and for expressions with unknown values.\n\n#### The Problem (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\n# In v1.9.0, sensitive marks could be lost in conditional expressions\nvariable \"is_prod\" {\n  type = bool\n}\n\nvariable \"database_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# Bug: The sensitive mark might be lost in this conditional\noutput \"password\" {\n  value = var.is_prod ? var.database_password : null\n  # Result might not be marked as sensitive!\n}\n```\n\n#### The Solution (v1.10.0)\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 combines marks from all values in conditional expressions to ensure consistency:\n\n```hcl\n# In v1.10.0, this now correctly preserves sensitive marks\noutput \"password\" {\n  value = var.is_prod ? var.database_password : null\n  # Result is correctly marked as sensitive regardless of the branch\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Impact\n\nThis is mostly **transparent** for users, but you might notice:\n\n1. **More values marked as sensitive**: If you were relying on the previous behavior where marks were lost, output may now show more `(sensitive value)` placeholders\n\n2. **Clearer intent**: Use `nonsensitive()` when you intentionally want to reveal a derived value:\n   ```hcl\n   # If you've derived a value that's safe to show\n   output \"hashed_password\" {\n     value = nonsensitive(bcrypt(var.database_password))\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **New conditional expression behavior**:\n   ```hcl\n   # Before: Might not be marked sensitive\n   output \"config\" {\n     value = var.include_secrets ? {\n       password = var.db_password\n     } : {}\n   }\n\n   # After: Correctly marked sensitive\n   # If var.db_password is sensitive, the entire map is sensitive\n   output \"config\" {\n     value = var.include_secrets ? {\n       password = var.db_password\n     } : {}\n     sensitive = true  # May need to add this now\n   }\n   ```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Review sensitive outputs**: Run `terraform plan` and look for outputs showing `(sensitive value)` where they didn't before\n\n2. **Add explicit `sensitive = true`** if needed:\n   ```hcl\n   output \"api_key\" {\n     value     = var.is_dev ? var.dev_key : var.prod_key\n     sensitive = true  # Both branches contain sensitive values\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Use `nonsensitive()` carefully** when a derived value is safe:\n   ```hcl\n   # Only use nonsensitive() when you're absolutely sure\n   output \"password_hash\" {\n     value = bcrypt(var.password)  # bcrypt result might not be sensitive\n     # Even though input was sensitive\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Test conditional branches**: Ensure both true and false branches are handled:\n   ```hcl\n   # Good: Both branches handle sensitivity\n   output \"value\" {\n     value = condition ? sensitive_value : null\n     sensitive = true  # Covers both cases\n   }\n\n   # Problem: False branch might not be sensitive\n   output \"value\" {\n     value = condition ? sensitive_value : \"default\"\n     sensitive = true  # Required now\n   }\n   ```\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Pre-Migration Checklist\n\n```bash\n# 1. Verify you're on v1.9.0\nterraform version\n\n# 2. Backup state\nterraform state pull > terraform.tfstate.backup\n\n# 3. Validate current configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# 4. Run plan to establish baseline\nterraform plan -out=baseline.plan\n```\n\n### Migration Process\n\n```bash\n# 1. Update Terraform version\n# Download v1.10.0 or use your version manager:\n# - tfenv: tfenv install 1.10.0 && tfenv use 1.10.0\n# - asdf:  asdf install terraform 1.10.0 && asdf local terraform 1.10.0\n\n# 2. Verify new version\nterraform version\n\n# 3. Validate configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# 4. Run plan with new version\nterraform plan -out=v1.10_plan\n\n# 5. Review plan for unexpected changes\n# Check for:\n# - Resource replacements\n# - Sensitive value changes\n# - New/removed attributes\n```\n\n### Post-Migration Validation\n\n```bash\n# 1. Verify state integrity\nterraform state list\nterraform state show resource.type.name\n\n# 2. Check for ephemeral value usage\nterraform console\n> var.my_ephemeral_var  # Should fail if not in ephemeral context\n\n# 3. Run integration tests\nterraform apply -auto-approve  # In non-prod environment\nterraform destroy -auto-approve\n\n# 4. Verify sensitive outputs\nterraform output\n# Should see (sensitive value) for outputs marked sensitive\n```\n\n### Specific Tests by Change Type\n\n#### For S3 Backend Migration\n```bash\n# 1. Test with old config (should fail)\nterraform init -upgrade\n\n# 2. Check that new config works\nterraform plan  # Should succeed\n\n# 3. Verify locking works\nterraform apply -auto-approve  # First process\n# In another terminal:\nterraform plan  # Should wait for lock\n\n# 4. Check lock file in S3\naws s3 ls s3://my-bucket/path/to/ | grep tflock\n```\n\n#### For Moved Blocks\n```bash\n# 1. Validate moved block syntax\nterraform validate\n\n# 2. Plan should show no changes\nterraform plan\n\n# 3. Apply should be a no-op\nterraform apply -auto-approve\n# Should show: No changes\n```\n\n#### For Ephemeral Values\n```bash\n# 1. Test ephemeral variable outside valid context (should fail)\n# terraform console\n# > resource.aws_instance.web.user_data  # Reference ephemeral var\n# Should error: \"ephemeralasnull\" required\n\n# 2. Test ephemeral variable in valid context (should succeed)\n# In ephemeral local or resource\nlocal \"my_val\" {\n  ephemeral = true\n  value = var.ephemeral_token\n}\n\n# 3. Verify ephemeral outputs not in state\nterraform state show module.child\n# Should NOT see ephemeral outputs\n\n# 4. Test with terraform console\nterraform console\n# Try to access ephemeral output: should fail\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### If You Need to Rollback to v1.9.0\n\n#### Step 1: Identify Rollback Point\n\n```bash\n# Find your last successful v1.9.0 plan/apply\ngit log --oneline | grep -i \"terraform\\|migration\"\n\n# Keep track of state version\nterraform state pull > state_v1.10.json\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Revert Configuration Changes\n\n```bash\n# Revert S3 backend to deprecated syntax\ngit checkout HEAD~N -- terraform/backend.tf\n\n# Revert moved blocks if they were changed\ngit checkout HEAD~N -- terraform/main.tf\n\n# Revert ephemeral value declarations\ngit checkout HEAD~N -- terraform/variables.tf\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Switch to v1.9.0\n\n```bash\n# Use your version manager\ntfenv install 1.9.0\ntfenv use 1.9.0\n\n# Verify version\nterraform version\n```\n\n#### Step 4: Validate and Plan\n\n```bash\n# Clear terraform cache\nrm -rf .terraform .terraform.lock.hcl\n\n# Reinitialize with v1.9.0\nterraform init\n\n# Validate configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# Review plan - should show NO changes\nterraform plan\n```\n\n#### Step 5: If Plan Shows Changes\n\n```bash\n# State mismatch occurred - need careful recovery\n# DO NOT apply the plan!\n\n# Option 1: Refresh state (safe)\nterraform refresh\n\n# Option 2: Restore from backup\nterraform state pull > terraform.tfstate.v1.10\nterraform state push terraform.tfstate.backup\n\n# Re-plan to verify\nterraform plan\n# Should now show no changes\n```\n\n### State Compatibility Notes\n\n- **States are compatible** between v1.9.0 and v1.10.0 in both directions\n- **No state migration** is required for the upgrade itself\n- **Moving back is possible** but configuration compatibility depends on what features you used\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Required Actions\n\n### Must Do (Breaking Changes)\n\n| Change | Action | Complexity |\n|--------|--------|-----------|\n| S3 Backend IAM attributes | Migrate to `assume_role` block | Medium |\n| Moved block syntax | Add `resource.` prefix to reserved keywords | Low |\n\n### Should Consider (Best Practices)\n\n| Feature | Action | Benefit |\n|---------|--------|---------|\n| Ephemeral variables | Replace `sensitive = true` with `ephemeral = true` for secrets | Better security - secrets never stored |\n| S3 native locking | Add `use_lockfile = true` | Eliminates DynamoDB dependency |\n| Sensitive handling | Review conditional expressions | Clearer, more consistent behavior |\n\n### Optional (New Capabilities)\n\n- Explore ephemeral resources for temporary infrastructure\n- Use `ephemeralasnull()` for flexible secret handling\n- Leverage new `terraform.applying` symbol in ephemeral contexts\n\n---\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### Error: \"Unsupported block type 'assume_role'\"\n\n**Cause**: Your S3 backend still uses root-level IAM attributes\n\n**Solution**: Wrap them in an `assume_role` block:\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    # Old way (broken in v1.10.0):\n    # role_arn = \"...\"\n\n    # New way:\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn = \"...\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Error: \"The address refers to a reserved keyword\"\n\n**Cause**: A `moved` block references a resource type matching a reserved keyword without `resource.` prefix\n\n**Solution**: Add `resource.` prefix:\n```hcl\n# Before (broken):\nmoved {\n  from = local.example\n  to   = aws_instance.web\n}\n\n# After (fixed):\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.example\n  to   = aws_instance.web\n}\n```\n\n### Error: \"Ephemeral variable referenced outside valid context\"\n\n**Cause**: Trying to use an ephemeral variable in a non-ephemeral context\n\n**Solution**: Either:\n1. Move the reference to a valid context (ephemeral resource, local, etc.)\n2. Use `ephemeralasnull()` to convert to non-ephemeral\n\n```hcl\n# Instead of this (fails):\n# resource.aws_instance.web.user_data = var.ephemeral_token\n\n# Do this:\nlocal \"temp\" {\n  ephemeral = true\n  value = var.ephemeral_token\n}\n\n# Or this:\noutput \"token\" {\n  ephemeral = true\n  value = var.ephemeral_token\n}\n```\n\n### State shows \"sensitive value\" where it didn't before\n\n**Cause**: New v1.10.0 behavior correctly preserves sensitive marks in conditional expressions\n\n**Solution**: This is expected. Either:\n1. Accept the `(sensitive value)` display\n2. Add `sensitive = true` to the output declaration\n3. Use `nonsensitive()` if the value is actually safe to display\n\n```hcl\noutput \"value\" {\n  value     = condition ? var.sensitive : null\n  sensitive = true  # Explicitly mark as sensitive\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n- [Terraform v1.10 Changelog](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [S3 Backend Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/backend/s3)\n- [Ephemeral Values Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/values/variables#exclude-values-from-state)\n- [Moved Block Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/modules/develop/refactoring)\n- [Terraform v1.0 Compatibility Promises](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1-compatibility-promises)\n\n---\n\n## Getting Help\n\nIf you encounter issues during migration:\n\n1. **Check Terraform logs**: `TF_LOG=DEBUG terraform plan`\n2. **Review the error message**: Usually very specific about what needs to change\n3. **Consult community forums**: [Terraform Community Forum](https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core)\n4. **Report bugs**: [GitHub Issues](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues)\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":11914,"cache_read_input_tokens":80119,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":11914},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"887ad210-ab51-4ddc-8bdb-d7f962f19408","uuid":"69a402ca-8fd6-4204-980c-1b419740e114"}
