While v1.10.0 honors the [Terraform v1.0 Compatibility Promises](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1-compatibility-promises), there are several breaking changes and behavioral modifications that require migration steps.\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces two major new features with migration implications:\n- **Ephemeral Resources and Values**: A new mechanism for handling secrets and temporary data that isn't persisted to state files\n- **Enhanced Sensitive Value Handling**: Improvements to how sensitive marks propagate through conditional and for expressions\n\nIt also includes breaking changes to the S3 backend and moved block syntax that require configuration updates.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Assumption Attributes\n\n#### What Changed and Why\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 **removes** the root-level IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend that were previously marked as deprecated. These attributes have been entirely removed in favor of the `assume_role` block syntax, which provides a cleaner, more organized way to configure role assumption.\n\n**Removed attributes:**\n- `role_arn`\n- `session_name`\n- `external_id`\n- `assume_role_duration_seconds`\n- `assume_role_policy`\n- `assume_role_policy_arns`\n- `assume_role_tags`\n- `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys`\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket                        = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key                           = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region                        = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table                = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    # DEPRECATED - These attributes must be migrated\n    role_arn                       = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n    session_name                   = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id                    = \"unique-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds   = 3600\n    assume_role_policy            = jsonencode({\n      Version = \"2012-10-17\"\n      Statement = [...]\n    })\n    assume_role_tags              = {\n      Environment = \"production\"\n    }\n    assume_role_transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    # Use the assume_role block instead\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn           = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n      session_name       = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id        = \"unique-external-id\"\n      duration           = \"1h\"  # Note: format changed from seconds to duration string\n      policy            = jsonencode({\n        Version = \"2012-10-17\"\n        Statement = [...]\n      })\n      policy_arn = [\n        \"arn:aws:iam::aws:policy/ReadOnlyAccess\"\n      ]\n      tags = {\n        Environment = \"production\"\n      }\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Back up your state file** before proceeding:\n   ```bash\n   terraform state pull > terraform.tfstate.backup\n   ```\n\n2. **Update your S3 backend configuration**:\n   - Remove all root-level `role_arn`, `session_name`, `external_id`, `assume_role_*` attributes\n   - Create an `assume_role` block containing the equivalent settings\n   - Convert `assume_role_duration_seconds` to duration format:\n     - `3600` (seconds) → `1h` (1 hour)\n     - Use format: `<hours>h<minutes>m<seconds>s`\n\n3. **Replace array attributes correctly**:\n   - `assume_role_policy_arns` (set) → `policy_arn` (list)\n   - `assume_role_tags` → `tags`\n\n4. **Validate your configuration**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform init\n   terraform validate\n   ```\n\n5. **Run a plan to ensure nothing changes unexpectedly**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Duration format**: Don't use raw seconds in the `duration` field - use the `1h` format instead\n- **Forgetting `assume_role` block**: If you remove the old attributes but don't add the `assume_role` block, Terraform will fail to initialize\n- **IAM permissions**: Ensure your IAM policies are updated to include `sts:AssumeRole` permissions for the role specified in `assume_role.role_arn`\n\n---\n\n### 2. S3 Backend: New S3 Native State Locking Support\n\n#### What Changed\n\nThe S3 backend now supports S3 native state locking as an **opt-in, experimental feature**. This allows locking state directly in S3 without requiring a separate DynamoDB table.\n\n#### Key Points\n\n- **Opt-in via `use_lockfile` parameter**: Set to `true` to enable S3 native locking\n- **Works alongside DynamoDB**: When both are configured, locks are acquired from both sources\n- **Lock file naming**: Lock files are stored with `.tflock` extension (e.g., `prod/terraform.tfstate.tflock`)\n- **IAM policy updates needed**: S3 bucket and IAM policies must be updated to include permissions for the lock files\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"  # Only option\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n**Option A: Use S3 native locking only (experimental)**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket       = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key          = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region       = \"us-east-1\"\n    use_lockfile = true  # New experimental feature\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Option B: Use both S3 and DynamoDB locking**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n    use_lockfile   = true  # Locks acquired from both sources\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps (Optional)\n\nTo adopt S3 native locking:\n\n1. **Update your S3 bucket policy** to include lock file permissions:\n   ```json\n   {\n     \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n     \"Statement\": [\n       {\n         \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n         \"Action\": [\n           \"s3:GetObject\",\n           \"s3:PutObject\",\n           \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n         ],\n         \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state/path/to/*.tflock\"\n       }\n     ]\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Update IAM policy** for your Terraform user/role:\n   ```json\n   {\n     \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n     \"Statement\": [\n       {\n         \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n         \"Action\": [\n           \"s3:GetObject\",\n           \"s3:PutObject\",\n           \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n         ],\n         \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state/path/to/*.tflock\"\n       }\n     ]\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Enable in your backend configuration**:\n   ```hcl\n   terraform {\n     backend \"s3\" {\n       # ... existing config ...\n       use_lockfile = true\n     }\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Run init and plan**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform init\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n#### Important Notes\n\n- This feature is **experimental** - behavior may change in future minor releases\n- DynamoDB-based locking will be deprecated in a future minor release\n- Both locking mechanisms can be used together for gradual migration\n\n---\n\n### 3. Moved Blocks: Syntax Changes for Reserved Keywords\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 enforces stricter parsing of resource addresses in `moved` blocks. Resources with type names that match reserved keywords (like `local`, `each`, `self`, `data`, `resource`, `module`, `variable`, `output`, `terraform`, `provider`) must now be prefixed with `resource.` to disambiguate them from the reserved keywords.\n\n#### Why This Matters\n\nPreviously, you could write:\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = local.my_resource\n  to   = aws_instance.web\n}\n```\n\nHowever, this creates ambiguity: Is `local` referring to a local value or a resource type named `local`? Terraform v1.10.0 requires explicit disambiguation.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\n# If you had a resource with type name matching a keyword\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  # ...\n}\n\n# This was ambiguous - did you mean the resource or the keyword?\nmoved {\n  from = local.config  # Ambiguous!\n  to   = aws_instance.web\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\n# Same resource\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  # ...\n}\n\n# Now you must be explicit\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.config  # Clear that this is a resource\n  to   = aws_instance.web\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Identify problematic `moved` blocks**: Check your configuration for `moved` blocks where the resource type matches a reserved keyword:\n   - `local`, `each`, `self`, `data`, `resource`, `module`, `variable`, `output`, `terraform`, `provider`\n\n2. **Add `resource.` prefix**: For any `from` or `to` addresses using reserved keyword resource types, prepend `resource.`:\n   ```hcl\n   # BEFORE\n   moved {\n     from = local.example\n     to   = aws_instance.web\n   }\n\n   # AFTER\n   moved {\n     from = resource.local.example\n     to   = aws_instance.web\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Validate your configuration**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   ```\n\n4. **Common reserved keywords to watch for**:\n   - `local` - Most common\n   - `data` - Data source type\n   - `resource` - Resource keyword\n   - `module` - Module keyword\n   - `variable`, `output` - Variable and output keywords\n   - `terraform`, `provider` - Meta-block keywords\n   - `each`, `self` - Built-in variables\n\n#### Example Scenario\n\nIf your codebase had custom providers with these type names:\n\n```hcl\n# Before migration - breaks in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = local.my_resource\n  to   = aws_instance.new_resource\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = data.old_config\n  to   = local_file.new_config\n}\n\n# After migration - works in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.my_resource\n  to   = aws_instance.new_resource\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = resource.data.old_config\n  to   = local_file.new_config\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### 4. Ephemeral Resources and Values\n\n#### What Are Ephemeral Values?\n\nEphemeral values are data that exists during Terraform operations but is **never stored** in plan files or state files. This is ideal for secrets, API tokens, and temporary credentials that should not persist beyond the current operation.\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n- **Not persisted**: Never written to `.tfstate` or plan files\n- **Temporary**: Available only during the current operation\n- **Contextual**: Can only be referenced in specific \"ephemeral contexts\"\n- **Secure by design**: Secrets are never at rest\n\n#### New Features in v1.10.0\n\n**1. Ephemeral Input Variables**\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_token\" {\n  type        = string\n  ephemeral   = true\n  description = \"Temporary API token that won't be stored in state\"\n}\n```\n\n**2. Ephemeral Outputs (in child modules)**\n```hcl\noutput \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  value       = aws_iam_access_key.temp.secret_access_key\n  ephemeral   = true\n  description = \"Temporary AWS secret key not stored in state\"\n}\n```\n\n**3. Ephemeral Resources**\n```hcl\nephemeral \"random_password\" \"temp\" {\n  length  = 32\n  special = true\n}\n```\n\n**4. `ephemeralasnull()` Function**\n```hcl\n# Convert ephemeral values to null for contexts where ephemeral isn't allowed\nlocal_file.config = {\n  content = ephemeralasnull(var.sensitive_config)\n}\n```\n\n#### Valid Contexts for Ephemeral Values\n\nEphemeral variables can only be referenced in:\n- Other ephemeral variables\n- Ephemeral local values\n- Ephemeral resources\n- Ephemeral outputs\n- `provider` blocks (for configuring providers)\n- `provisioner` and `connection` blocks\n\n#### Migration Considerations\n\n**If you currently use `sensitive` for secrets:**\n```hcl\n# v1.9.0 approach - secrets stored in state (marked as sensitive in output)\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true  # Hidden in output, but still in state\n}\n```\n\n**Consider migrating to ephemeral if the secret never needs to be stored:**\n```hcl\n# v1.10.0 approach - secrets never stored at all\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type        = string\n  ephemeral   = true  # Not stored in state or plan\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps for Ephemeral Values\n\n1. **Identify secrets that don't need persistence**: Look for resources/variables that only need to exist during execution\n2. **Mark them as ephemeral** where appropriate:\n   ```hcl\n   # Before\n   variable \"temporary_token\" {\n     type      = string\n     sensitive = true\n   }\n\n   # After\n   variable \"temporary_token\" {\n     type      = string\n     ephemeral = true\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Update references to respect ephemeral contexts**: If you reference ephemeral values outside of valid contexts, use `ephemeralasnull()`:\n   ```hcl\n   resource \"aws_instance\" \"web\" {\n     # This would fail - can't use ephemeral variable directly here\n     # user_data = var.temp_token\n\n     # Instead, handle gracefully\n     user_data = base64encode(ephemeralasnull(var.temp_token) ?? \"\")\n   }\n   ```\n\n#### Important Notes\n\n- **Ephemeral is in public beta**: Workflows are subject to change\n- **Root module limitation**: You cannot mark outputs as ephemeral in the root module\n- **Ephemeral outputs are child-module only**: Can only be used to pass values between modules, not persisted to root module state\n\n---\n\n### 5. Sensitive Value Handling in Conditional Expressions\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 **improves the consistency** of how sensitive marks propagate through conditional expressions. Previously, sensitive marks could be lost in certain combinations of conditional and for expressions with unknown values.\n\n#### The Problem (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\n# In v1.9.0, sensitive marks could be lost in conditional expressions\nvariable \"is_prod\" {\n  type = bool\n}\n\nvariable \"database_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# Bug: The sensitive mark might be lost in this conditional\noutput \"password\" {\n  value = var.is_prod ? var.database_password : null\n  # Result might not be marked as sensitive!\n}\n```\n\n#### The Solution (v1.10.0)\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 combines marks from all values in conditional expressions to ensure consistency:\n\n```hcl\n# In v1.10.0, this now correctly preserves sensitive marks\noutput \"password\" {\n  value = var.is_prod ? var.database_password : null\n  # Result is correctly marked as sensitive regardless of the branch\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Impact\n\nThis is mostly **transparent** for users, but you might notice:\n\n1. **More values marked as sensitive**: If you were relying on the previous behavior where marks were lost, output may now show more `(sensitive value)` placeholders\n\n2. **Clearer intent**: Use `nonsensitive()` when you intentionally want to reveal a derived value:\n   ```hcl\n   # If you've derived a value that's safe to show\n   output \"hashed_password\" {\n     value = nonsensitive(bcrypt(var.database_password))\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **New conditional expression behavior**:\n   ```hcl\n   # Before: Might not be marked sensitive\n   output \"config\" {\n     value = var.include_secrets ? {\n       password = var.db_password\n     } : {}\n   }\n\n   # After: Correctly marked sensitive\n   # If var.db_password is sensitive, the entire map is sensitive\n   output \"config\" {\n     value = var.include_secrets ? {\n       password = var.db_password\n     } : {}\n     sensitive = true  # May need to add this now\n   }\n   ```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Review sensitive outputs**: Run `terraform plan` and look for outputs showing `(sensitive value)` where they didn't before\n\n2. **Add explicit `sensitive = true`** if needed:\n   ```hcl\n   output \"api_key\" {\n     value     = var.is_dev ? var.dev_key : var.prod_key\n     sensitive = true  # Both branches contain sensitive values\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Use `nonsensitive()` carefully** when a derived value is safe:\n   ```hcl\n   # Only use nonsensitive() when you're absolutely sure\n   output \"password_hash\" {\n     value = bcrypt(var.password)  # bcrypt result might not be sensitive\n     # Even though input was sensitive\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Test conditional branches**: Ensure both true and false branches are handled:\n   ```hcl\n   # Good: Both branches handle sensitivity\n   output \"value\" {\n     value = condition ? sensitive_value : null\n     sensitive = true  # Covers both cases\n   }\n\n   # Problem: False branch might not be sensitive\n   output \"value\" {\n     value = condition ? sensitive_value : \"default\"\n     sensitive = true  # Required now\n   }\n   ```\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Pre-Migration Checklist\n\n```bash\n# 1. Verify you're on v1.9.0\nterraform version\n\n# 2. Backup state\nterraform state pull > terraform.tfstate.backup\n\n# 3. Validate current configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# 4. Run plan to establish baseline\nterraform plan -out=baseline.plan\n```\n\n### Migration Process\n\n```bash\n# 1. Update Terraform version\n# Download v1.10.0 or use your version manager:\n# - tfenv: tfenv install 1.10.0 && tfenv use 1.10.0\n# - asdf:  asdf install terraform 1.10.0 && asdf local terraform 1.10.0\n\n# 2. Verify new version\nterraform version\n\n# 3. Validate configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# 4. Run plan with new version\nterraform plan -out=v1.10_plan\n\n# 5. Review plan for unexpected changes\n# Check for:\n# - Resource replacements\n# - Sensitive value changes\n# - New/removed attributes\n```\n\n### Post-Migration Validation\n\n```bash\n# 1. Verify state integrity\nterraform state list\nterraform state show resource.type.name\n\n# 2. Check for ephemeral value usage\nterraform console\n> var.my_ephemeral_var  # Should fail if not in ephemeral context\n\n# 3. Run integration tests\nterraform apply -auto-approve  # In non-prod environment\nterraform destroy -auto-approve\n\n# 4. Verify sensitive outputs\nterraform output\n# Should see (sensitive value) for outputs marked sensitive\n```\n\n### Specific Tests by Change Type\n\n#### For S3 Backend Migration\n```bash\n# 1. Test with old config (should fail)\nterraform init -upgrade\n\n# 2. Check that new config works\nterraform plan  # Should succeed\n\n# 3. Verify locking works\nterraform apply -auto-approve  # First process\n# In another terminal:\nterraform plan  # Should wait for lock\n\n# 4. Check lock file in S3\naws s3 ls s3://my-bucket/path/to/ | grep tflock\n```\n\n#### For Moved Blocks\n```bash\n# 1. Validate moved block syntax\nterraform validate\n\n# 2. Plan should show no changes\nterraform plan\n\n# 3. Apply should be a no-op\nterraform apply -auto-approve\n# Should show: No changes\n```\n\n#### For Ephemeral Values\n```bash\n# 1. Test ephemeral variable outside valid context (should fail)\n# terraform console\n# > resource.aws_instance.web.user_data  # Reference ephemeral var\n# Should error: \"ephemeralasnull\" required\n\n# 2. Test ephemeral variable in valid context (should succeed)\n# In ephemeral local or resource\nlocal \"my_val\" {\n  ephemeral = true\n  value = var.ephemeral_token\n}\n\n# 3. Verify ephemeral outputs not in state\nterraform state show module.child\n# Should NOT see ephemeral outputs\n\n# 4. Test with terraform console\nterraform console\n# Try to access ephemeral output: should fail\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### If You Need to Rollback to v1.9.0\n\n#### Step 1: Identify Rollback Point\n\n```bash\n# Find your last successful v1.9.0 plan/apply\ngit log --oneline | grep -i \"terraform\\|migration\"\n\n# Keep track of state version\nterraform state pull > state_v1.10.json\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Revert Configuration Changes\n\n```bash\n# Revert S3 backend to deprecated syntax\ngit checkout HEAD~N -- terraform/backend.tf\n\n# Revert moved blocks if they were changed\ngit checkout HEAD~N -- terraform/main.tf\n\n# Revert ephemeral value declarations\ngit checkout HEAD~N -- terraform/variables.tf\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Switch to v1.9.0\n\n```bash\n# Use your version manager\ntfenv install 1.9.0\ntfenv use 1.9.0\n\n# Verify version\nterraform version\n```\n\n#### Step 4: Validate and Plan\n\n```bash\n# Clear terraform cache\nrm -rf .terraform .terraform.lock.hcl\n\n# Reinitialize with v1.9.0\nterraform init\n\n# Validate configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# Review plan - should show NO changes\nterraform plan\n```\n\n#### Step 5: If Plan Shows Changes\n\n```bash\n# State mismatch occurred - need careful recovery\n# DO NOT apply the plan!\n\n# Option 1: Refresh state (safe)\nterraform refresh\n\n# Option 2: Restore from backup\nterraform state pull > terraform.tfstate.v1.10\nterraform state push terraform.tfstate.backup\n\n# Re-plan to verify\nterraform plan\n# Should now show no changes\n```\n\n### State Compatibility Notes\n\n- **States are compatible** between v1.9.0 and v1.10.0 in both directions\n- **No state migration** is required for the upgrade itself\n- **Moving back is possible** but configuration compatibility depends on what features you used\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Required Actions\n\n### Must Do (Breaking Changes)\n\n| Change | Action | Complexity |\n|--------|--------|-----------|\n| S3 Backend IAM attributes | Migrate to `assume_role` block | Medium |\n| Moved block syntax | Add `resource.` prefix to reserved keywords | Low |\n\n### Should Consider (Best Practices)\n\n| Feature | Action | Benefit |\n|---------|--------|---------|\n| Ephemeral variables | Replace `sensitive = true` with `ephemeral = true` for secrets | Better security - secrets never stored |\n| S3 native locking | Add `use_lockfile = true` | Eliminates DynamoDB dependency |\n| Sensitive handling | Review conditional expressions | Clearer, more consistent behavior |\n\n### Optional (New Capabilities)\n\n- Explore ephemeral resources for temporary infrastructure\n- Use `ephemeralasnull()` for flexible secret handling\n- Leverage new `terraform.applying` symbol in ephemeral contexts\n\n---\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### Error: \"Unsupported block type 'assume_role'\"\n\n**Cause**: Your S3 backend still uses root-level IAM attributes\n\n**Solution**: Wrap them in an `assume_role` block:\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    # Old way (broken in v1.10.0):\n    # role_arn = \"...\"\n\n    # New way:\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn = \"...\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Error: \"The address refers to a reserved keyword\"\n\n**Cause**: A `moved` block references a resource type matching a reserved keyword without `resource.` prefix\n\n**Solution**: Add `resource.` prefix:\n```hcl\n# Before (broken):\nmoved {\n  from = local.example\n  to   = aws_instance.web\n}\n\n# After (fixed):\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.example\n  to   = aws_instance.web\n}\n```\n\n### Error: \"Ephemeral variable referenced outside valid context\"\n\n**Cause**: Trying to use an ephemeral variable in a non-ephemeral context\n\n**Solution**: Either:\n1. Move the reference to a valid context (ephemeral resource, local, etc.)\n2. Use `ephemeralasnull()` to convert to non-ephemeral\n\n```hcl\n# Instead of this (fails):\n# resource.aws_instance.web.user_data = var.ephemeral_token\n\n# Do this:\nlocal \"temp\" {\n  ephemeral = true\n  value = var.ephemeral_token\n}\n\n# Or this:\noutput \"token\" {\n  ephemeral = true\n  value = var.ephemeral_token\n}\n```\n\n### State shows \"sensitive value\" where it didn't before\n\n**Cause**: New v1.10.0 behavior correctly preserves sensitive marks in conditional expressions\n\n**Solution**: This is expected. Either:\n1. Accept the `(sensitive value)` display\n2. Add `sensitive = true` to the output declaration\n3. Use `nonsensitive()` if the value is actually safe to display\n\n```hcl\noutput \"value\" {\n  value     = condition ? var.sensitive : null\n  sensitive = true  # Explicitly mark as sensitive\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n- [Terraform v1.10 Changelog](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [S3 Backend Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/backend/s3)\n- [Ephemeral Values Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/values/variables#exclude-values-from-state)\n- [Moved Block Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/modules/develop/refactoring)\n- [Terraform v1.0 Compatibility Promises](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1-compatibility-promises)\n\n---\n\n## Getting Help\n\nIf you encounter issues during migration:\n\n1. **Check Terraform logs**: `TF_LOG=DEBUG terraform plan`\n2. **Review the error message**: Usually very specific about what needs to change\n3. **Consult community forums**: [Terraform Community Forum](https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core)\n4. **Report bugs**: [GitHub Issues](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues)\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
